  <raw>Town set to benefit




 CHORLEY MP Lindsay Hoyle co-hosted the Westminster launch of a new partnership designed to improve the productivity of North West aerospace companies.



 The collaboration between the North West Aerospace Alliance (NWAA) and the Society of British Aerospace Companies (SBAC) should greatly benefit local companies in Chorley as well as the North West.


 The aims of the link are to raise skill levels, provide a catalyst for innovation and improve industry supply chains, all key in the challenging global market place.

 Mr Hoyle's launch speech revolved around the need to match the skills young people acquire at college with the requirements of the world beating aerospace companies in the North West.

 He said: "Work-based degrees and qualifications can help to ensure the needs of industry are met by universities."

 The aerospace industry is a significant employer in the North West supporting more than 60,000 jobs.

 It also produces around ?6.8 billion in aerospace output each year.

 SBAC president, Kevin Smith, said: "I am delighted that the North West Aerospace Alliance has become the SBAC's Regional Partner."

 The partnership was announced to MPs at a special reception in the Atlee Suite, in the House of Commons.

 Representatives of leading aerospace companies attended the presentation, those present including Airbus, BAE Systems, Rolls-Royce plc, Bombardier and Thales UK.</raw>
